# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir`

# Grafana Dashboard Schema Version Migration Pipeline

## Your Task

Find all Go and TypeScript source files in grafana/grafana that implement the dashboard JSON schema version migration pipeline. Identify: the migration runner (apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/), the versioned migration function registry (GetMigrations returning version-to-function map), individual migration steps (e.g. V2, V36), and the frontend DashboardMigrator in TypeScript that mirrors the backend logic.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the dashboard JSON schema version migration pipeline in grafana/grafana. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components

**Backend (Go)**:
- **Migration Runner** (`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go`): Orchestrates the migration process through `Initialize()` and `Migrate()` functions
- **Migration Registry** (`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go`): `GetMigrations()` function returns a map of version numbers to migration functions
- **Individual Migrations** (v2.go through v42.go): 41 migration files implementing each schema version transformation
- **Utilities** (`migration_utils.go`): Type conversion and data access helpers

**Frontend (TypeScript)**:
- **DashboardMigrator Class** (`public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`): Mirrors backend logic with `updateSchema()` method implementing all 41 schema migrations
- **DashboardModel** (`public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardModel.ts`): Integrates DashboardMigrator for automatic schema migration on dashboard load

**Supporting Files**:
- Conversion layer (`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/`): API-level conversions with metrics
- Documentation (`README.md`, `schemaversion/README.md`): Comprehensive guides for implementation and testing

The migration system transforms dashboards sequentially from their input version to the latest (v42), with both backend and frontend implementations ensuring consistency. Each version migration has dedicated test files validating correctness.

The complete findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all files, key symbols, and the full migration chain documented.

[Available metrics](#available-metrics)\\n31: - [Related Documentation](#related-documentation)\\n32: \\n33: ## Overview\\n34: \\n35: The Grafana dashboard migration system operates across three main conversion layers:\\n36: \\n37: ### Conversion Flow: v0 \u2192 v1 \u2192 v2\\n38: \\n39: ```\\n40: v0alpha1 (Legacy JSON) \u2192 v1beta1 (Migrated JSON) \u2192 v2alpha1/v2beta1 (Structured)\\n41: ```\\n42: \\n43: #### v0 to v1 Conversion:\\n44: - All schema migrations (v0-v42) are executed in the backend\\n45: - Ports the logic from DashboardMigrator and implements built-in plugin migrations for panel plugins since backend cannot load plugins\\n46: - Transforms legacy JSON dashboards to migrated JSON format\\n47: - Handles backward compatibility for older dashboard formats\\n48: - See [SchemaVersion Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md) for detailed instructions on creating new schema migrations\\n49: \\n50: #### v1 to v2 Conversion:\\n51: - API version conversions between different Kubernetes API versions\\n52: - Transforms JSON dashboards to structured dashboard format\\n53: - v2 schema is the stable, typed schema with proper type definitions\\n54: - Handles modern dashboard features and Kubernetes-native storage\\n55: \\n56: ## Conversion Matrix\\n57: \\n58: The system supports conversions between all dashboard API versions:\\n59: \\n60: | From \u2193 / To \u2192 | v0alpha1 | v1beta1 | v2alpha1 | v2beta1 |\\n61: |---------------|----------|---------|----------|---------|\\n62: | **v0alpha1**  | \u2713        | \u2713       | \u2713        | \u2713       |\\n63: | **v1beta1**   | \u2713        | \u2713       | \u2713        | \u2713       |\\n64: | **v2alpha1**  | \u2713        | \u2713       | \u2713        | \u2713       |\\n65: | **v2beta1**   | \u2713        | \u2713       | \u2713        | \u2713       |\\n66: \\n67: Each conversion path is automatically instrumented with metrics and logging.\\n68: \\n69: ## API Versions\\n70: \\n71: The supported dashboard API versions are:\\n72: \\n73: - `dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1` - Legacy JSON dashboard format\\n74: - `dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1` - Migrated JSON dashboard format  \\n75: - `dashboard.grafana.app/v2alpha1` - New structured dashboard format\\n76: - `dashboard.grafana.app/v2beta1` - Enhanced structured dashboard format\\n77: \\n78: ## Schema Versions\\n79: \\n80: Schema versions (v13-v42) apply only to v0alpha1 and v1beta1 dashboards:\\n81: \\n82: - **Minimum supported version**: v13\\n83: - **Latest version**: v42  \\n84: - **Migration path**: Sequential (v13\u2192v14\u2192v15...\u2192v42)\\n85: \\n86: For detailed information about creating schema version migrations, see the [SchemaVersion Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md).\\n87: \\n88: ## Testing\\n89: \\n90: The implementation includes comprehensive test coverage for conversion-level operations:\\n91: \\n92: - **Backend conversion tests**: API version conversions with metrics validation\\n93: - **Frontend tests**: TypeScript conversion tests  \\n94: - **Integration tests**: End-to-end conversion validation\\n95: - **Metrics tests**: Prometheus counter validation\\n96: \\n97: ### Backend conversion tests\\n98: \\n99: The backend conversion tests validate API version conversions and metrics instrumentation:\\n100: \\n101: - **API conversion tests**: Test conversions between v0alpha1, v1beta1, v2alpha1, v2beta1\\n102: - **Metrics validation**: Tests verify that conversion metrics are properly recorded\\n103: - **Error handling**: Tests validate error classification and logging\\n104: - **Performance**: Tests ensure conversion operations are efficient\\n105: \\n106: **Test execution:**\\n107: ```bash\\n108: # All backend conversion tests\\n109: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/... -v\\n110: \\n111: # Metrics validation tests\\n112: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestSchemaMigrationMetrics\\n113: ```\\n114: \\n115: ### Frontend migration comparison tests\\n116: \\n117: The frontend migration comparison tests validate that backend and frontend conversion logic produce consistent results:\\n118: \\n119: - **Test methodology**: Compares backend vs frontend conversion outputs through DashboardModel integration\\n120: - **Dataset coverage**: Tests run against curated test files covering various conversion scenarios\\n121: - **Test location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts`\\n122: - **Test data**: Located in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/testdata/input/` and `testdata/output/`\\n123: \\n124: **Test execution:**\\n125: ```bash\\n126: # Frontend migration comparison tests\\n127: yarn test DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts\\n128: ```\\n129: \\n130: **Test approach:**\\n131: - **Frontend path**: `jsonInput \u2192 DashboardModel \u2192 DashboardMigrator \u2192 getSaveModelClone()`\\n132: - **Backend path**: `jsonInput \u2192 Backend Conversion \u2192 backendOutput \u2192 DashboardModel \u2192 getSaveModelClone()`\\n133: - **Comparison**: Direct comparison of final converted states from both paths\\n134: \\n135: For schema version migration testing details, see the [SchemaVersion Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md).\\n136: \\n137: ## Monitoring Migrations\\n138: \\n139: The dashboard migration system provides comprehensive observability through metrics, logging, and error classification to monitor conversion operations.\\n140: \\n141: ### Metrics\\n142: \\n143: The dashboard migration system now provides comprehensive observability through:\\n144: - **Prometheus metrics** for tracking conversion success/failure rates and performance\\n145: - **Structured logging** for debugging and monitoring conversion operations\\n146: - **Automatic instrumentation** via wrapper functions that eliminate code duplication\\n147: - **Error classification** to distinguish between different types of migration failures\\n148: \\n149: #### 1. Dashboard conversion success metric\\n150: \\n151: **Metric Name:** `grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_success_total`\\n152: \\n153: **Type:** Counter\\n154: \\n155: **Description:** Total number of successful dashboard conversions\\n156: \\n157: **Labels:**\\n158: - `source_version_api` - Source API version (e.g., \\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\\\")\\n159: - `target_version_api` - Target API version (e.g., \\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\\\")\\n160: - `source_schema_version` - Source schema version (e.g., \\\"16\\\") - only for v0/v1 dashboards\\n161: - `target_schema_version` - Target schema version (e.g., \\\"41\\\") - only for v0/v1 dashboards\\n162: \\n163: **Example:**\\n164: ```prometheus\\n165: grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_success_total{\\n166:   source_version_api=\\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\\\",\\n167:   target_version_api=\\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\\\",\\n168:   source_schema_version=\\\"16\\\",\\n169:   target_schema_version=\\\"41\\\"\\n170: } 1250\\n171: ```\\n172: \\n173: #### 2. Dashboard conversion failure metric\\n174: \\n175: **Metric Name:** `grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_failure_total`\\n176: \\n177: **Type:** Counter\\n178: \\n179: **Description:** Total number of failed dashboard conversions\\n180: \\n181: **Labels:**\\n182: - `source_version_api` - Source API version\\n183: - `target_version_api` - Target API version  \\n184: - `source_schema_version` - Source schema version (only for v0/v1 dashboards)\\n185: - `target_schema_version` - Target schema version (only for v0/v1 dashboards)\\n186: - `error_type` - Classification of the error (see Error Types section)\\n187: \\n188: **Example:**\\n189: ```prometheus\\n190: grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_failure_total{\\n191:   source_version_api=\\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\\\",\\n192:   target_version_api=\\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\\\",\\n193:   source_schema_version=\\\"14\\\",\\n194:   target_schema_version=\\\"41\\\",\\n195:   error_type=\\\"schema_version_migration_error\\\"\\n196: } 42\\n197: ```\\n198: \\n199: ### Error Types\\n200: \\n201: The `error_type` label classifies failures into three categories:\\n202: \\n203: #### 1. `conversion_error`\\n204: - General conversion failures not related to schema migration\\n205: - API-level conversion issues\\n206: - Programming errors in conversion functions\\n207: \\n208: #### 2. `schema_version_migration_error`\\n209: - Failures during individual schema version migrations (v14\u2192v15, v15\u2192v16, etc.)\\n210: - Schema-specific transformation errors\\n211: - Data format incompatibilities\\n212: \\n213: #### 3. `schema_minimum_version_error`\\n214: - Dashboards with schema versions below the minimum supported version (< v13)\\n215: - These are logged as warnings rather than errors\\n216: - Indicates dashboards that cannot be migrated automatically\\n217: \\n218: ### Logging\\n219: \\n220: #### Log structure\\n221: \\n222: All migration logs use structured logging with consistent field names:\\n223: \\n224: **Base Fields (always present):**\\n225: - `sourceVersionAPI` - Source API version\\n226: - `targetVersionAPI` - Target API version\\n227: - `dashboardUID` - Unique identifier of the dashboard being converted\\n228: \\n229: **Schema Version Fields (v0/v1 dashboards only):**\\n230: - `sourceSchemaVersion` - Source schema version number\\n231: - `targetSchemaVersion` - Target schema version number\\n232: - `erroredSchemaVersionFunc` - Name of the schema migration function that failed (on error)\\n233: \\n234: **Error Fields (failures only):**\\n235: - `errorType` - Same classification as metrics error_type label\\n236: - `erroredConversionFunc` - Name of the conversion function that failed\\n237: - `error` - The actual error message\\n238: \\n239: #### Log levels\\n240: \\n241: ##### Success (DEBUG level)\\n242: ```json\\n243: {\\n244:   \\\"level\\\": \\\"debug\\\",\\n245:   \\\"msg\\\": \\\"Dashboard conversion succeeded\\\",\\n246:   \\\"sourceVersionAPI\\\": \\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\\\",\\n247:   \\\"targetVersionAPI\\\": \\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\\\",\\n248:   \\\"dashboardUID\\\": \\\"abc123\\\",\\n249:   \\\"sourceSchemaVersion\\\": 16,\\n250:   \\\"targetSchemaVersion\\\": 41\\n251: }\\n252: ```\\n253: \\n254: ##### Conversion/Migration Error (ERROR level)\\n255: ```json\\n256: {\\n257:   \\\"level\\\": \\\"error\\\", \\n258:   \\\"msg\\\": \\\"Dashboard conversion failed\\\",\\n259:   \\\"sourceVersionAPI\\\": \\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\\\",\\n260:   \\\"targetVersionAPI\\\": \\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\\\",\\n261:   \\\"erroredConversionFunc\\\": \\\"Convert_V0_to_V1\\\",\\n262:   \\\"dashboardUID\\\": \\\"abc123\\\",\\n263:   \\\"sourceSchemaVersion\\\": 16,\\n264:   \\\"targetSchemaVersion\\\": 41,\\n265:   \\\"erroredSchemaVersionFunc\\\": \\\"V24\\\",\\n266:   \\\"errorType\\\": \\\"schema_version_migration_error\\\",\\n267:   \\\"error\\\": \\\"migration failed: table panel plugin not found\\\"\\n268: }\\n269: ```\\n270: \\n271: ##### Minimum Version Error (WARN level)\\n272: ```json\\n273: {\\n274:   \\\"level\\\": \\\"warn\\\",\\n275:   \\\"msg\\\": \\\"Dashboard conversion failed\\\", \\n276:   \\\"sourceVersionAPI\\\": \\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\\\",\\n277:   \\\"targetVersionAPI\\\": \\\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\\\",\\n278:   \\\"erroredConversionFunc\\\": \\\"Convert_V0_to_V1\\\",\\n279:   \\\"dashboardUID\\\": \\\"def456\\\",\\n280:   \\\"sourceSchemaVersion\\\": 10,\\n281:   \\\"targetSchemaVersion\\\": 41,\\n282:   \\\"erroredSchemaVersionFunc\\\": \\\"\\\",\\n283:   \\\"errorType\\\": \\\"schema_minimum_version_error\\\",\\n284:   \\\"error\\\": \\\"dashboard schema version 10 cannot be migrated\\\"\\n285: }\\n286: ```\\n287: \\n288: ### Implementation Details\\n289: \\n290: #### Automatic instrumentation\\n291: \\n292: All dashboard conversions are automatically instrumented via the `withConversionMetrics` wrapper function:\\n293: \\n294: ```go\\n295: // All conversion functions are wrapped automatically\\n296: s.AddConversionFunc((*dashv0.Dashboard)(nil), (*dashv1.Dashboard)(nil),\\n297:     withConversionMetrics(dashv0.APIVERSION, dashv1.APIVERSION, func(a, b interface{}, scope conversion.Scope) error {\\n298:         return Convert_V0_to_V1(a.(*dashv0.Dashboard), b.(*dashv1.Dashboard), scope)\\n299:     }))\\n300: ```\\n301: \\n302: #### Error handling\\n303: \\n304: Custom error types provide structured error information:\\n305: \\n306: ```go\\n307: // Schema migration errors\\n308: type MigrationError struct {\\n309:     msg            string\\n310:     targetVersion  int\\n311:     currentVersion int\\n312:     functionName   string\\n313: }\\n314: \\n315: // API conversion errors  \\n316: type ConversionError struct {\\n317:     msg               string\\n318:     functionName      string\\n319:     currentAPIVersion string\\n320:     targetAPIVersion  string\\n321: }\\n322: ```\\n323: \\n324: ### Registration\\n325: \\n326: #### Metrics registration\\n327: \\n328: Metrics must be registered with Prometheus during service initialization:\\n329: \\n330: ```go\\n331: import \\\"github.com/grafana/grafana/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration\\\"\\n332: \\n333: // Register metrics with Prometheus\\n334: migration.RegisterMetrics(prometheusRegistry)\\n335: ```\\n336: \\n337: #### Available metrics\\n338: \\n339: The following metrics are available after registration:\\n340: \\n341: ```go\\n342: // Success counter\\n343: migration.MDashboardConversionSuccessTotal\\n344: \\n345: // Failure counter  \\n346: migration.MDashboardConversionFailureTotal\\n347: ```\\n348: \\n349: ## Related Documentation\\n350: \\n351: - [Schema Migration Guide](./schemaversion/README.md) - Complete guide for creating new dashboard schema migrations\\n352: - [PR #110178 - Dashboard migration: Add missing metrics registration](https://github.com/grafana/grafana/pull/110178)\\n353: **Error classification** to distinguish between different types of migration failures\n148: \n149: #### 1. Dashboard conversion success metric\n150: \n151: **Metric Name:** `grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_success_total`\n152: \n153: **Type:** Counter\n154: \n155: **Description:** Total number of successful dashboard conversions\n156: \n157: **Labels:**\n158: - `source_version_api` - Source API version (e.g., \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\")\n159: - `target_version_api` - Target API version (e.g., \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\")\n160: - `source_schema_version` - Source schema version (e.g., \"16\") - only for v0/v1 dashboards\n161: - `target_schema_version` - Target schema version (e.g., \"41\") - only for v0/v1 dashboards\n162: \n163: **Example:**\n164: ```prometheus\n165: grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_success_total{\n166:   source_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n167:   target_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n168:   source_schema_version=\"16\",\n169:   target_schema_version=\"41\"\n170: } 1250\n171: ```\n172: \n173: #### 2. Dashboard conversion failure metric\n174: \n175: **Metric Name:** `grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_failure_total`\n176: \n177: **Type:** Counter\n178: \n179: **Description:** Total number of failed dashboard conversions\n180: \n181: **Labels:**\n182: - `source_version_api` - Source API version\n183: - `target_version_api` - Target API version  \n184: - `source_schema_version` - Source schema version (only for v0/v1 dashboards)\n185: - `target_schema_version` - Target schema version (only for v0/v1 dashboards)\n186: - `error_type` - Classification of the error (see Error Types section)\n187: \n188: **Example:**\n189: ```prometheus\n190: grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_failure_total{\n191:   source_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n192: ```\n198: \n199: ### Error Types\n200: \n201: The `error_type` label classifies failures into three categories:\n202: \n203: #### 1. `conversion_error`\n204: - General conversion failures not related to schema migration\n205: - API-level conversion issues\n206: - Programming errors in conversion functions\n207: \n208: #### 2. `schema_version_migration_error`\n209: - Failures during individual schema version migrations (v14\u2192v15, v15\u2192v16, etc.)\n210: - Schema-specific transformation errors\n211: - Data format incompatibilities\n212: \n213: #### 3. `schema_minimum_version_error`\n214: - Dashboards with schema versions below the minimum supported version (< v13)\n215: - These are logged as warnings rather than errors\n216: - Indicates dashboards that cannot be migrated automatically\n217: \n218: ### Logging\n219: \n220: #### Log structure\n221: \n222: All migration logs use structured logging with consistent field names:\n223: \n224: **Base Fields (always present):**\n225: - `sourceVersionAPI` - Source API version\n226: - `targetVersionAPI` - Target API version\n227: - `dashboardUID` - Unique identifier of the dashboard being converted\n228: \n229: **Schema Version Fields (v0/v1 dashboards only):**\n230: - `sourceSchemaVersion` - Source schema version number\n231: - `targetSchemaVersion` - Target schema version number\n232: - `erroredSchemaVersionFunc` - Name of the schema migration function that failed (on error)\n233: \n234: **Error Fields (failures only):**\n235: - `errorType` - Same classification as metrics error_type label\n236: - `erroredConversionFunc` - Name of the conversion function that failed\n237: - `error` - The actual error message\n238: \n239: #### Log levels\n240: \n241: ##### Success (DEBUG level)\n242: ```json\n243: {\n244:   \"level\": \"debug\",\n245:   \"msg\": \"Dashboard conversion succeeded\",\n246:   \"sourceVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n247:   \"targetVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n248:   \"dashboardUID\": \"abc123\",\n249:   \"sourceSchemaVersion\": 16,\n250:   \"targetSchemaVersion\": 41\n251: }\n252: ```\n253: \n254: [Frontend Migration Comparison Tests](#frontend-migration-comparison-tests)\\n32:   - [Single Version Migration Testing](#single-version-migration-testing)\\n33: - [Resources](#resources)\\n34: - [Getting Help](#getting-help)\\n35: \\n36: ## Overview\\n37: \\n38: Dashboard schema migrations ensure backward compatibility as the dashboard data model evolves. Each migration transforms dashboards from one schema version to the next, allowing older dashboards to work with newer Grafana versions.\\n39: \\n40: ## Current Schema Versions\\n41: \\n42: - **Minimum Version**: 13\\n43: - **Latest Version**: 42\\n44: - **Backend Location**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/`\\n45: - **Frontend Location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`\\n46: \\n47: ## Creating a New Migration\\n48: \\n49: ### Step 1: Create the Migration File\\n50: \\n51: Create a new file: `v{N}.go` where `{N}` is the target schema version.\\n52: \\n53: ```go\\n54: package schemaversion\\n55: \\n56: import \\\"context\\\"\\n57: \\n58: // V{N} migrates [describe what this migration does].\\n59: //\\n60: // [Detailed description of the migration including:]\\n61: // - What properties are being changed\\n62: // - Why the migration is necessary\\n63: // - Any special handling or edge cases\\n64: //\\n65: // Example before migration:\\n66: //\\n67: //\\t\\\"panels\\\": [\\n68: //\\t  {\\n69: //\\t    \\\"id\\\": 1,\\n70: //\\t    \\\"type\\\": \\\"graph\\\",\\n71: //\\t    \\\"oldProperty\\\": \\\"value\\\"\\n72: //\\t  }\\n73: //\\t]\\n74: //\\n75: // Example after migration:\\n76: //\\n77: //\\t\\\"panels\\\": [\\n78: //\\t  {\\n79: //\\t    \\\"id\\\": 1,\\n80: //\\t    \\\"type\\\": \\\"graph\\\",\\n81: //\\t    \\\"newProperty\\\": \\\"value\\\"\\n82: //\\t  }\\n83: //\\t]\\n84: func V{N}(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {\\n85: \\tdashboard[\\\"schemaVersion\\\"] = {N}\\n86: \\n87: \\t// Your migration logic here\\n88: \\t// Transform dashboard properties as needed\\n89: \\n90: \\treturn nil\\n91: }\\n92: ```\\n93: \\n94: ### Step 2: Register the Migration\\n95: \\n96: Add your migration to `migrations.go`:\\n97: \\n98: ```go\\n99: func GetMigrations(dsInfoProvider DataSourceInfoProvider) map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc {\\n100: \\treturn map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc{\\n101: \\t\\t// ... existing migrations\\n102: \\t\\t{N}: V{N},  // Add your migration here\\n103: \\t\\t// ... rest of migrations\\n104: \\t}\\n105: }\\n106: ```\\n107: \\n108: ### Step 3: Create Test Data\\n109: \\n110: #### Input Test File\\n111: Create `testdata/input/v{N}.{name}.json` with schema version `{N-1}` with scenarios to cover the specific migration:\\n112: \\n113: ```json\\n114: {\\n115:   \\\"title\\\": \\\"V{N} Migration Test Dashboard\\\",\\n116:   \\\"schemaVersion\\\": {N-1},\\n117:   \\\"panels\\\": [\\n118:     {\\n119:       \\\"id\\\": 1,\\n120:       \\\"type\\\": \\\"graph\\\",\\n121:       \\\"title\\\": \\\"Test Panel\\\",\\n122:       \\\"oldProperty\\\": \\\"value\\\"\\n123:     }\\n124:   ]\\n125: }\\n126: ```\\n127: \\n128: #### Expected Output\\n129: The test system will generate `testdata/output/latest_version/v{N}.{name}.v42.json` automatically.\\n130: \\n131: ### Step 4: Run Tests\\n132: \\n133: ```bash\\n134: # Run migration tests\\n135: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/...\\n136: \\n137: # Run specific migration test\\n138: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\\n139: ```\\n140: \\n141: For comprehensive testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\\n142: \\n143: ### Step 5: Frontend-Backend Consistency Validation\\n144: \\n145: Implement different changes in the migration until frontend matches exactly with the backend side. Add as many scenarios as possible to ensure comprehensive coverage of all use cases.\\n146: \\n147: For detailed testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\\n148: \\n149: #### Test Scenarios to Cover\\n150: \\n151: **Panel-Level Changes:**\\n152: - Panels with different types (graph, table, stat, etc.)\\n153: - Panels with nested panels (rows)\\n154: - Panels with various property combinations\\n155: - Panels with missing or null properties\\n156: - Panels with deprecated properties\\n157: \\n158: **Dashboard-Level Changes:**\\n159: - Dashboard properties (title, tags, time, etc.)\\n160: - Templating variables (query, textbox, custom, etc.)\\n161: - Annotations and links\\n162: - Time picker settings\\n163: - Refresh settings\\n164: \\n165: **Edge Cases:**\\n166: - Empty dashboards\\n167: - Dashboards with only rows\\n168: - Dashboards with mixed panel types\\n169: - Dashboards with complex nested structures\\n170: - Dashboards with invalid or malformed data\\n171: \\n172: **Property Transformations:**\\n173: - Property renaming scenarios\\n174: - Property type conversions\\n175: - Property value transformations\\n176: - Property removal scenarios\\n177: - Property addition scenarios\\n178: \\n179: #### Validation Process\\n180: \\n181: 1. **Create comprehensive test data** covering all scenarios\\n182: 2. **Run backend migration** and capture output\\n183: 3. **Run frontend migration** and capture output\\n184: 4. **Compare outputs** using strict equality checks\\n185: 5. **Iterate on migration logic** until outputs match exactly\\n186: 6. **Add more test cases** for any discrepancies found\\n187: \\n188: #### Test Data Requirements\\n189: \\n190: Create multiple test files for each migration:\\n191: - `v{N}.basic.{name}.json` - Basic functionality\\n192: - `v{N}.edge_cases.{name}.json` - Edge cases and error conditions\\n193: - `v{N}.complex.{name}.json` - Complex dashboard structures\\n194: - `v{N}.property_changes.{name}.json` - Property transformation scenarios\\n195: \\n196: ### Step 6: Unit Testing\\n197: \\n198: Add comprehensive unit tests for both backend and frontend migrations to ensure the correct logic is implemented.\\n199: \\n200: #### Backend Unit Tests\\n201: \\n202: Create unit tests in `v{N}_test.go`:\\n203: \\n204: ```go\\n205: package schemaversion_test\\n206: \\n207: import (\\n208: \\t\\\"context\\\"\\n209: \\t\\\"testing\\\"\\n210: \\t\\\"github.com/stretchr/testify/require\\\"\\n211: \\t\\\"github.com/grafana/grafana/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion\\\"\\n212: )\\n213: \\n214: func TestV{N}(t *testing.T) {\\n215: \\ttests := []struct {\\n216: \\t\\tname     string\\n217: \\t\\tinput    map[string]interface{}\\n218: \\t\\texpected map[string]interface{}\\n219: \\t}{\\n220: \\t\\t{\\n221: \\t\\t\\tname: \\\"basic property migration\\\",\\n222: \\t\\t\\tinput: map[string]interface{}{\\n223: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"schemaVersion\\\": {N-1},\\n224: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"panels\\\": []interface{}{\\n225: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tmap[string]interface{}{\\n226: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"id\\\": 1,\\n227: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"type\\\": \\\"graph\\\",\\n228: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"oldProperty\\\": \\\"value\\\",\\n229: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n230: \\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n231: \\t\\t\\t},\\n232: \\t\\t\\texpected: map[string]interface{}{\\n233: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"schemaVersion\\\": {N},\\n234: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"panels\\\": []interface{}{\\n235: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tmap[string]interface{}{\\n236: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"id\\\": 1,\\n237: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"type\\\": \\\"graph\\\",\\n238: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"newProperty\\\": \\\"value\\\",\\n239: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n240: \\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n241: \\t\\t\\t},\\n242: \\t\\t},\\n243: \\t\\t{\\n244: \\t\\t\\tname: \\\"edge case - missing property\\\",\\n245: \\t\\t\\tinput: map[string]interface{}{\\n246: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"schemaVersion\\\": {N-1},\\n247: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"panels\\\": []interface{}{\\n248: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tmap[string]interface{}{\\n249: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"id\\\": 1,\\n250: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"type\\\": \\\"graph\\\",\\n251: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n252: \\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n253: \\t\\t\\t},\\n254: \\t\\t\\texpected: map[string]interface{}{\\n255: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"schemaVersion\\\": {N},\\n256: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"panels\\\": []interface{}{\\n257: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tmap[string]interface{}{\\n258: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"id\\\": 1,\\n259: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"type\\\": \\\"graph\\\",\\n260: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n261: \\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n262: \\t\\t\\t},\\n263: \\t\\t},\\n264: \\t\\t// Add more test cases...\\n265: \\t}\\n266: \\n267: \\tfor _, tt := range tests {\\n268: \\t\\tt.Run(tt.name, func(t *testing.T) {\\n269: \\t\\t\\terr := schemaversion.V{N}(context.Background(), tt.input)\\n270: \\t\\t\\trequire.NoError(t, err)\\n271: \\t\\t\\trequire.Equal(t, tt.expected, tt.input)\\n272: \\t\\t})\\n273: \\t}\\n274: }\\n275: ```\\n276: \\n277: #### Frontend Unit Tests\\n278: \\n279: Create unit tests in `DashboardMigrator.test.ts`:\\n280: \\n281: ```typescript\\n282: describe('V{N} Migration', () => {\\n283:   it('should migrate basic property changes', () => {\\n284:     const dashboard = {\\n285:       schemaVersion: {N-1},\\n286:       panels: [\\n287:         {\\n288:           id: 1,\\n289:           type: 'graph',\\n290:           oldProperty: 'value'\\n291:         }\\n292:       ]\\n293:     };\\n294: \\n295:     const model = new DashboardModel(dashboard);\\n296:     expect(model.schemaVersion).toBe({N});\\n297:     expect(model.panels[0].newProperty).toBe('value');\\n298:     expect(model.panels[0].oldProperty).toBeUndefined();\\n299:   });\\n300: \\n301:   it('should handle edge cases correctly', () => {\\n302:     const dashboard = {\\n303:       schemaVersion: {N-1},\\n304:       panels: []\\n305:     };\\n306: \\n307:     const model = new DashboardModel(dashboard);\\n308:     expect(model.schemaVersion).toBe({N});\\n309:     expect(model.panels).toEqual([]);\\n310:   });\\n311: \\n312:   // Add more test cases...\\n313: });\\n314: ```\\n315: \\n316: \\n317: #### Running Unit Tests\\n318: \\n319: ```bash\\n320: # Backend unit tests\\n321: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/... -run TestV{N}\\n322: \\n323: # Frontend unit tests\\n324: yarn test DashboardMigrator.test.ts -t \\\"V{N}\\\"\\n325: \\n326: # Integration tests\\n327: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\\n328: yarn test DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts\\n329: ```\\n330: \\n331: \\n332: \\n333: ## Utility Functions\\n334: \\n335: ### Type Conversion\\n336: ```go\\n337: // Convert various types to float64\\n338: func ConvertToFloat(value interface{}) (float64, bool) {\\n339: \\t// Implementation in utils.go\\n340: }\\n341: \\n342: // Get string value with default\\n343: func GetStringValue(data map[string]interface{}, key string, defaultValue string) string {\\n344: \\t// Implementation in utils.go\\n345: }\\n346: \\n347: // Get boolean value with default\\n348: func GetBoolValue(data map[string]interface{}, key string) bool {\\n349: \\t// Implementation in utils.go\\n350: }\\n351: ```\\n352: \\n353: ### Data Access\\n354: ```go\\n355: // Safe property access\\n356: if value, ok := panel[\\\"property\\\"].(string); ok {\\n357: \\t// Use value\\n358: }\\n359: \\n360: // Safe array access\\n361: if panels, ok := dashboard[\\\"panels\\\"].([]interface{}); ok {\\n362: \\t// Process panels\\n363: }\\n364: ```\\n365: \\n366: ## Common Pitfalls\\n367: \\n368: ### 1. Type Assertions\\n369: ```go\\n370: // \u274c Wrong - can panic\\n371: value := panel[\\\"property\\\"].(string)\\n372: \\n373: // \u2705 Correct - safe type assertion\\n374: if value, ok := panel[\\\"property\\\"].(string); ok {\\n375: \\t// Use value\\n376: }\\n377: ```\\n378: \\n379: ### 2. Null Handling\\n380: ```go\\n381: // \u274c Wrong - removes intentional nulls\\n382: if value == nil {\\n383: \\tdelete(panel, \\\"property\\\")\\n384: }\\n385: \\n386: // \u2705 Correct - preserve intentional nulls\\n387: if value == nil && !isIntentionallyNull(panel, \\\"property\\\") {\\n388: \\tdelete(panel, \\\"property\\\")\\n389: }\\n390: ```\\n391: \\n392: ### 3. Nested Panel Processing\\n393: ```go\\n394: // \u274c Wrong - misses nested panels\\n395: for _, panel := range panels {\\n396: \\tmigratePanel(panel)\\n397: }\\n398: \\n399: // \u2705 Correct - handles nested panels\\n400: for _, panel := range panels {\\n401: \\tmigratePanelRecursively(panel)\\n402: }\\n403: ```\\n404: \\n405: ## Migration Beyond v42\\n406: \\n407: **Important**: Schema version 42 is the final version for the v1 dashboard API. For new migrations beyond v42:\\n408: \\n409: 1. **Backend**: Continue adding schema versions in Go\\n410: 2. **Frontend**: Use panel-specific migration handlers instead of schema versions\\n411: 3. **Justification Required**: Each new migration must be properly justified\\n412: 4. **v2 Transition**: Consider the impact on the transition to schema v2\\n413: \\n414: ### When to Add Schema Migrations vs Panel Migrations\\n415: \\n416: **Add Schema Migration** when:\\n417: - Changes affect dashboard-level properties\\n418: - Cross-panel transformations are needed\\n419: - Backward compatibility requires schema version increment\\n420: - **With proper justification** about why it can't be handled as panel migration\\n421: \\n422: **Use Panel-Specific Migrations** when:\\n423: - Changes are panel-type specific\\n424: - Can be handled within individual panel plugins\\n425: - Don't require dashboard-level schema changes\\n426: \\n427: ## Testing Guidelines\\n428: \\n429: ### Test File Naming\\n430: - Input: `v{N}.{descriptive_name}.json`\\n431: - Output: `v{N}.{descriptive_name}.v42.json`\\n432: \\n433: ### Test Data Requirements\\n434: - Input schema version should be `{N-1}`\\n435: - Include comprehensive test cases\\n436: - Test edge cases and error conditions\\n437: - Use realistic dashboard data\\n438: \\n439: ### Running Tests\\n440: ```bash\\n441: # Run all migration tests\\n442: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/...\\n443: \\n444: # Run specific test\\n445: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\\n446: \\n447: # Run with verbose output\\n448: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -v\\n449: ```\\n450: \\n451: ## Comprehensive Testing Strategy\\n452: \\n453: ### Backend Migration Tests\\n454: \\n455: The backend migration tests validate schema version migrations and API conversions:\\n456: \\n457: - **Schema migration tests**: Test individual schema version upgrades (v14\u2192v15, v15\u2192v16, etc.)\\n458: - **Conversion tests**: Test API version conversions with automatic metrics instrumentation\\n459: - **Test data**: Uses curated test files from `testdata/input/` covering schema versions 14-42\\n460: - **Metrics validation**: Tests verify that conversion metrics are properly recorded\\n461: \\n462: **Test execution:**\\n463: ```bash\\n464: # All backend migration tests\\n465: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -v\\n466: \\n467: # Schema migration tests only\\n468: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/ -v\\n469: \\n470: # API conversion tests with metrics\\n471: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/... -v\\n472: ```\\n473: \\n474: ### Frontend Migration Comparison Tests\\n475: \\n476: The frontend migration comparison tests validate that backend and frontend migration logic produce consistent results:\\n477: \\n478: - **Test methodology**: Compares backend vs frontend migration outputs through DashboardModel integration\\n479: - **Dataset coverage**: Tests run against 42+ curated test files spanning schema versions 14-42\\n480: - **Test location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts`\\n481: - **Test data**: Located in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/testdata/input/` and `testdata/output/`\\n482: \\n483: **Test execution:**\\n484: ```bash\\n485: # Frontend migration comparison tests\\n486: yarn test DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts\\n487: ```\\n488: \\n489: **Test approach:**\\n490: - **Frontend path**: `jsonInput \u2192 DashboardModel \u2192 DashboardMigrator \u2192 getSaveModelClone()`\\n491: - **Backend path**: `jsonInput \u2192 Backend Migration \u2192 backendOutput \u2192 DashboardModel \u2192 getSaveModelClone()`\\n492: - **Comparison**: Direct comparison of final migrated states from both paths\\n493: \\n494: ### Single Version Migration Testing\\n495: \\n496: The system supports both single version and full pipeline testing:\\n497: \\n498: - **Single version tests**: Test individual migrations (v15 \u2192 v16)\\n499: - **Full pipeline tests**: Test complete migration (v15 \u2192 v42)\\n500: - **Test directories**: `single_version/` vs `latest_version/`\\n501: - **Coverage**: Comprehensive testing of all migration paths\\n502: \\n503: **Test execution:**\\n504: ```bash\\n505: # Single version migration tests\\n506: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrateSingleVersion\\n507: \\n508: # Full pipeline tests\\n509: go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\\n510: ```\\n511: \\n512: ## Resources\\n513: \\n514: - The `Migrate()` function serves as the entry point, coordinating the entire migration process. It calls `Initialize()` to set up dependencies and manages the sequential application of schema version migrations from the input version to the target version.\\n\\n**Migration Function Registry**: The `GetMigrations()` function in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go` (lines 36-80) returns a map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc containing all registered migrations, keyed by version number. Notable examples include:\\n- V33(dsInfoProvider) - Takes a DataSourceInfoProvider dependency\\n- V36(dsInfoProvider) - Migrates datasource references from legacy string format to structured UID-based objects\\n- Standard migrations: V2 through V42\\n\\n**Individual Migration Steps**: Each schema version has a dedicated implementation file (v2.go through v42.go) in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/`. Backend receives a dashboard JSON with schema version V (e.g., v39)\\n2. `Migrate()` calls `GetMigrations()` to get the registry\\n3.
